<div id="review_1349116489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349116489" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349116489?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14066678-christina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349116489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11206307496949619336"><b>
  <i>Original Read: Nov. 6th - Nov. 14th, 2015<br/>Re-read: May 28th - June 4th, 2017</i>
</b><br/><br/>I loved this just as much the second time reading it. My original review and thoughts remain the same.<br/><br/>*******************************<br/>Original Review:<br/><br/><i>4.5 stars</i><br/><br/><b>"Once upon a time, there was a girl who lived in a kingdom of death. Wolves howled up her arm. A whole pack of them -- made of tattoo ink and pain, memory and loss. It was the only thing about her that ever stayed the same."</b><br/><br/>What if the Axis had won World War 2?<br/>It</span>
  <span id="freeText11206307496949619336" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Original Read: Nov. 6th - Nov. 14th, 2015<br />Re-read: May 28th - June 4th, 2017</i>
</b><br /><br />I loved this just as much the second time reading it. My original review and thoughts remain the same.<br /><br />*******************************<br />Original Review:<br /><br /><i>4.5 stars</i><br /><br /><b>"Once upon a time, there was a girl who lived in a kingdom of death. Wolves howled up her arm. A whole pack of them -- made of tattoo ink and pain, memory and loss. It was the only thing about her that ever stayed the same."</b><br /><br />What if the Axis had won World War 2?<br />It's a scary question to contemplate. Most historians concede that it was, at some point or another, possible. Alternative history is a genre composed of educated guesswork and speculation. That's what Ryan Graudin bases this novel on. That and a little dose of the mythical. <br />I admit to being the geeky kid who was morbidly fascinated by random points and events in<br />history....WW2 and the Holocaust being one of those periods of history. So, of course, I adore historical fiction. I will still never get over the atrocities that humans can be capable of, in the past and even now in the present day. It makes me so sad that people can't learn from the mistakes of those in the past and continue to do such horrible things to each other.<br /><br /><b>"Tonight death is at Hitler's door. And I am the one to bear it.<br />I have always been the one to bear it."</b><br /><br />The year is 1956 and the Axis powers of the Third Reich and Imperial Japan rule. To commemorate their great victory, they host the Axis Tour : an annual motorcycle race across their conjoined continents. The prize? An audience with the highly reclusive Adolf Hitler at the Victor's Ball in Tokyo.<br />Yael, a former death camp prisoner, has witnessed too much suffering, and the five wolves tattooed on her arm are a constant reminder of the loved ones she has lost. The resistance has given Yael one goal: win the race and kill Hitler. <br /><br /><b>"Her bullets and blade were for three things: defense, coercion and the Fuhrer's chest."</b><br /><br />A survivor of painful human experimentation, Yael has the power to skinshift and must complete her mission by impersonating last years only female racer, Adele Wolfe. This deception becomes more difficult when Felix, Adele's twin brother, and Luka, her former love interest, enter the race and watch Yael's every move. <br /><br /><b>"Not everything was gray ashfall, yellowing weeds, withered blue hands, crimson rivers of blood....There was still beauty in this world. And it was worth fighting for."</b><br /><br />The author has said that this book, at its heart, is about identity. What makes people who they are? The color of their skin? The blood in their veins? I love that she gave her MC the ability to skinshift as a way to confront this dilemma. No matter who Yael impersonated, what her outward appearance, she was still the same girl. The same girl who's world was torn apart and never really put back together completely. I loved that through it all, Yael never lost who she was in the way that mattered, though she feared that she had lost herself long ago when her ability to skinshift led to her forgetting her true appearance. But after all, that's not what matters. The author did a beautiful job of reinforcing that all people are created equal, despite race, despite gender, despite everything. Would rec to everyone to read and I am so, so incredibly happy that this isn't going to be a standalone. I cannot wait to see what happens in the next chapter of Yael's life, in the world that I am so happy didn't come to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11206307496949619336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16489521652372124326">Holy. Fuck. <br/><br/>Amber recommended this book to me in December last year and I bought it back in January but it's been sitting on my shelf ever since. I had no real inclination to pick it up and I honestly didn't know what the hell this book was about. <br/><br/>I decided randomly yesterday that I would finally read this book and man I wish I had picked it up sooner!   <span id="freeText16489521652372124326" style="display:none">Holy. Fuck. <br /><br />Amber recommended this book to me in December last year and I bought it back in January but it's been sitting on my shelf ever since. I had no real inclination to pick it up and I honestly didn't know what the hell this book was about. <br /><br />I decided randomly yesterday that I would finally read this book and man I wish I had picked it up sooner! This book wasn't what I expected - although, to be fair, I didn't know what to expect. Even though there's a motorbike on the front cover, I didn't realise there would be a motorbike race as the main feature of the book. It kinda made me a bit hesitant to read it when I discovered this since it was totally not my thing. However, I quickly became absolutely HOOKED by this book. I couldn't put it down for a second and I ended up staying up late to read as much as possible before I had to sleep. <br /><br />I'm so blown away by this book and I can't wait to read Blood for Blood! Yael is an amazing main character and I totally fell for Luka throughout this book. I need <b>more</b> asap!</span>

<div id="review_1497611405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497611405" />
    <a title="Clara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22197507-clara"><img alt="Clara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587553128p2/22197507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497611405?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clara" href="/user/show/22197507-clara">Clara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22197507-clara?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22197507-clara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22197507-clara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22197507-clara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497611405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7138764259808335675"><b>** 4 “I NEED THE SECOND BOOK NOW !!” **</b><br/><br/>I don’t understand why I waited so long to read this, especially because the synopsis had always appealed to me, but I don’t know, I never came around to read it in the end until now ! And what an amazing read this was !! Loved it !<br/><br/> <b>
  <u> The story and world-building : </u>
</b> <br/>•	Basically, I loved the whole concept of the book : writing a story about our world as it could have been <b> IF Hitler had won WW2</b>. Just this aspect alone was <b>fascinating</b> and had a way to make</span>
  <span id="freeText7138764259808335675" style="display:none"><b>** 4 “I NEED THE SECOND BOOK NOW !!” **</b><br /><br />I don’t understand why I waited so long to read this, especially because the synopsis had always appealed to me, but I don’t know, I never came around to read it in the end until now ! And what an amazing read this was !! Loved it !<br /><br /> <b>
  <u> The story and world-building : </u>
</b> <br />•	Basically, I loved the whole concept of the book : writing a story about our world as it could have been <b> IF Hitler had won WW2</b>. Just this aspect alone was <b>fascinating</b> and had a way to make it appear more <b>realistic</b> because it’s inspired directly from true events that have taken place not so long ago, <b>touching you</b> more deeply and more personally than any other dystopian story could, because you know this could have been real. <br />•	Now on to the other aspect of the story : the <b>motorcycle race</b> ! Badass much ?! The entire book revolves around a group of teenagers from both the Third Reich and the Japanese Empire competing in a motorcycle race going from Germany through North Africa and China to Japan, in the span of 3 weeks. The whole thing just made the book <b> action-packed, thrilling and fast-paced </b>, making you feel as if you were on a bike of your own with the other competitors. <br />•	I also really enjoyed the back and forth between the <b>present</b>, meaning the race, and the <b>past</b>of Yael, what happened to her in the camp that gave her the ability to skinshift and how she lost all the people she loved and cared for leading to her absolute hatred of Hitler and giving more <b> meaning to her mission </b> of killing him. <br />•	The added <b>fantasy element</b> of the story through Yael’s <b>skinshifting</b> was in my opinion accurate and spot-on to deal with the antisemitism under Hitler’s reign. <br /><br />I never got bored on bit while reading and was <b>hooked</b> from the first <b> words weaved so beautifully </b> and with such <b>meaning</b> and <b>feeling</b> by the author. She managed to deal smoothly and with the right words with serious subjects such as the Holocaust or the issue of identity very present in this book. <br /><br /><b>
  <u> The characters :</u>
</b><br />•	I really liked the main character, <i>
  <b>Yael</b>
</i>. I liked how <b>badass</b> and <b>brave</b> she was, but without being arrogant about it which I found quite enjoyable. Despite that, Yael still had <b>insecurities and doubts</b>, making her feel so humane, and making you feel closer to her due to that. I liked how the author dealt with the issue of identity through Yael’s character and her skinshifting : Yael’s constant fear of losing herself and who she truly is inside behind the faces and identities that she stole and used. <br />•	I guess my <b>only complaint</b> about this book, and the reason why I didn’t give the book five stars, was because I wasn’t very fond of the second main character, <i>
  <b>Luka </b>
</i>. He’s shown from the start as an <b>arrogant and pompous</b> guy, trying to be funny when actually he’s not. I thought his character felt sometimes <b>too forced</b> and not natural. In my eyes, he only appeared as a cliché cocky love interest that didn’t really have anything interesting about him. I can’t say I hated him, but he just didn’t make me feel anything. I especially didn’t really feel the connection between him and Yael, and the fact that he apparently loved the real Adele in the first place makes it hard for me to believe he could love the real Yael. <br />•	However, I really liked <i>
  <b>Felix</b>
</i>, Adele’s brother. He’s such a <b> caring, protective and selfless brother </b>, despite Yael-Adele hitting him or lying to him, he was always there for his sister, and I found that very touching. I liked that even though Felix thought Yael was his sister, Yael still found someone she could count on and maybe even trust. <br /><br />As for the ending, it was very surprising and awesome, and now I really don’t know what to expect from book 2 which is good, and I can’t wait !!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7138764259808335675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I love alternate histories and this was just phenomenal. The writing, characters, plot, execution, everything was so so so well done. I recommend this book to everyone everywhere GO READ IT!! So excited to see where this story goes from here!! Can't wait to get my hands on the next book when it comes out!!</span>

<div id="review_1512612409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1512612409" />
    <a title="Lonna | FLYLēF" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42319420-lonna-flyl-f"><img alt="Lonna | FLYLēF" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431746518p2/42319420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1512612409?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lonna | FLYLēF" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lonna | FLYLēF" href="/user/show/42319420-lonna-flyl-f">Lonna | FLYLēF</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42319420-lonna-flyl-f?shelf=2016-challenge">2016-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1512612409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2075736706273824065"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432224148i/14910585.png' alt='FLYLēF Book Reviews' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Original Post: <a href='http://reviews.flylef.com/2016/03/wolf-by-wolf.html' target='_new' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>Wolf by Wolf</em>
</a> at <a href='http://www.flylef.com/' target='_new' rel='nofollow noopener'>FLYLēF</a> (<a href='http://www.flylef.com/' target='_new' rel='nofollow noopener'>www.flylef.com</a>)<br/><br/>HISTORY IS REVIVED to magnificent effects in this moving and haunting novel. Ryan Graudin’s <em>Wolf by Wolf</em> shines a light on one of the darkest, most terrifying chapters in our past and spins a remarkable tale of an alternate history. The <em>what-if’s</em> set in motion by one courageous girl—Yael Adele— had me racing along, and rooting for her to change history as we know it: Win the Axis Tour. Assassinate Hitler.<br/><br/><em>Or Die Trying.</em><br/><br/>Graudin’s writing is</span>
  <span id="freeText2075736706273824065" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432224148i/14910585.png" alt="FLYLēF Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Original Post: <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2016/03/wolf-by-wolf.html" target="_new" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Wolf by Wolf</em>
</a> at <a href="http://www.flylef.com/" target="_new" rel="nofollow noopener">FLYLēF</a> (<a href="http://www.flylef.com/" target="_new" rel="nofollow noopener">www.flylef.com</a>)<br><br>HISTORY IS REVIVED to magnificent effects in this moving and haunting novel. Ryan Graudin’s <em>Wolf by Wolf</em> shines a light on one of the darkest, most terrifying chapters in our past and spins a remarkable tale of an alternate history. The <em>what-if’s</em> set in motion by one courageous girl—Yael Adele— had me racing along, and rooting for her to change history as we know it: Win the Axis Tour. Assassinate Hitler.<br><br><em>Or Die Trying.</em><br><br>Graudin’s writing is very lyrical. There is a musicality to her prose that is quite rhythmic—like a song, like a chant. The playful effects of typefaces and font sizes — faint, fainter, faintest — are so successful in enhancing the story. I know most people won’t look twice at this, but as a designer I enjoy and appreciate the extra attention to these details.<br><br>The characters are written so well. They possess qualities that I genuinely thrive on: strength through struggle, flawed not foolish, and an overall “<em>more</em>ness.” Yael is an impersonator, resistance conspirator, black-market scoundrel—a secret weapon. “You are special. You are going to change things.” My fondness for Yael grows with every flashback that the author takes me on, and I had this aching need to hug her. She is an incredible story of fortitude, identity, and destiny.<br><br>As Yael sets her eyes on winning the Axis Tour, twenty contestants stand in her path. My favorites among them are Luka, an ally and romantic interest who is as charismatic as he is deadly; Felix, her brother and wild card; and Katsu, who will stop at nothing to win the coveted and illusive Axis Tour Double Cross. These characters have an overall “<em>more</em>ness” that was never boring. I was questioning their motives and loyalty until the end.<br><br>I followed along with them on a mad dash from Germainia to Tokyo, covering 39,731,284 kilometers (okay, it was actually 20,780…still). The bit of sabotaging between the competitors breaks the monotony of the race, but each incident resolved itself fairly quickly. Personally, I’m really not fond of dirt-bike racing, so I ended up skimming those parts; however, I did gain a greater appreciation for it. Thank you Mr. David (supportive husband) for taking Ms. Graudin off road on a surprise dirt-bike date. I’m sure it is because of this experience that I was able to feel the bumps and bruises, aches and soreness, as Yael led me to an exciting climax that unraveled at lightning speed, leaving me with a burning need for the sequel—<em>Blood for Blood</em>. Is November here yet? No. Oh <em>Scheisse</em>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2075736706273824065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3492593587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3492593587" />
    <a title="Arunima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27283906-arunima"><img alt="Arunima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598720527p2/27283906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3492593587?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arunima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arunima" href="/user/show/27283906-arunima">Arunima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=aty-challenge-2020">aty-challenge-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=popsugar-challenge-2020">popsugar-challenge-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=my-heart">my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=historic-fictions">historic-fictions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=ww2">ww2</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3492593587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7081081680282869626"><b> *4.5 stars* </b><br/><br/><blockquote> <i>“Once upon a different time, there was a girl who lived in a kingdom of death. Wolves howled up her arm. A whole pack of them--made of tattoo ink and pain, memory and loss. It was the only thing about her that ever stayed the same.<br/>Her story begins on a train.” </i> </blockquote><br/><br/><b>Wolf by Wolf- <i>An alternate history laced with action, thrill, betrayal, loss and desperation, all threaded together brilliantly to deliver an incredible tale.</i> </b> A tale of a girl, who was no girl at all. A girl who had lost he</span>
  <span id="freeText7081081680282869626" style="display:none"><b> *4.5 stars* </b><br /><br /><blockquote> <i>“Once upon a different time, there was a girl who lived in a kingdom of death. Wolves howled up her arm. A whole pack of them--made of tattoo ink and pain, memory and loss. It was the only thing about her that ever stayed the same.<br />Her story begins on a train.” </i> </blockquote><br /><br /><b>Wolf by Wolf- <i>An alternate history laced with action, thrill, betrayal, loss and desperation, all threaded together brilliantly to deliver an incredible tale.</i> </b> A tale of a girl, who was no girl at all. A girl who had lost her own face behind numerous foreign faces. A girl with so many identities but not one of her own. A girl who has lost all that she loved. A girl who has lost but remembers all. Forces herself to remember each and every pain and loss. Because she has to. She has to remember the pain, for the rage to follow it, <b> because with that very rage brewing, curdling, brimming inside of her, <i>she is going to put a bullet through the Führer. </i> </b><br /><br /><blockquote> Babushka—the one who gave her purpose.<br />Mama—the one who gave her life.<br />Miriam—the one who gave her freedom.<br />Aaron-Klaus—the one who gave her a mission.<br />Vlad—the one who gave her pain.<br /><br /><i>These were the names she whispered in the dark.<br />These were the pieces she brought back into place.<br />These were the wolves she rode to war.</i> </blockquote><br /><br />I was really excited by the premise of this story which is of an alternate universe-more like, alternate history. <b>Wolf by Wolf is built on an alternate history where World War II ended with the victory of the Axis power.</b> But that's not the only point where Ryan Graudin deviates from the events of the real world. Back in the day in Nazi Germany, there were a series of gruesome genetic experiments carried out on Jews at the concentration camps. <br /><br />I was aware of the fact that these heartless experiments had existed which had inflicted ghastly things on their subjects but I wasn't aware of what actually these said ghastly things were and the extent of them. So I went and read a bit about these experiments and realized how much more brutal these experiments had been than I had presumed in my head - sewing twin babies to create conjoined twins, injecting dyes into the eyes, mutilation without anesthesia, freezing bodies to see means to prevent and treat hypothermia, and just so many more sickening things. However, most of these experiments failed and resulted in the death of most subjects. <br /><br />Ryan Graudin takes this element from reality and constructs her story further from a situation where one of these experiments leads to a very different, highly unprecedented outcome. Yael was six when she and her mother were forced into a train full of other victims and shipped to one of the camps. There, among thousands of other similar kids like her, she was picked as the <i> chosen one.</i> Chosen for one of the most "special experiments ever. For years she was injected with strange fluids, resulting in days of severe pain, fever, and just so much torture. Her skin had started to shed, change colours in patches. She wasn't herself anymore. She was slowly coming undone, peeling away. <i>She finally loses her own face, her own body but realizes she has the ability to take any other.</i> <b>Years of experimentation had resulted in her having the ability to skin shift, be anyone at all. </b><br /><br />Now it's the year 1956 and Yael is a part of the resistance with the biggest mission of her life. The fate of the entire country lies on her shoulders. She must win this year's Axis Tour- the annual motorcycle race across the entire conquered area of The Third Reich and Imperial Japan- disguised as last year victor's, Adele Wolfe. Then after that, the plan is simple- get invited to the Victor's ball, share a dance with Hitler and then put a bullet through his heart. <br /><br />However, when she enters the race, she realizes disguising as Adele isn't as simple as she had hoped for it to be for there are two boys-Felix, Adele's brother and Luka, a fellow victor who appears to share this secret history with Adele which seems to have gone down terribly - intent on keep throwing at her a past that she didn't share with them, that she has no idea of, posing as a threat to her guarded secrets, a threat to her entire mission. There is a slight romance in it which would possibly bloom more in the next book though I am not sure how that would play out, if at all it does. Well, we will find that out soon enough. I have the sequel beside me (hehehe).<br /><br /><b>The entire time, I was high on an adrenalin rush, scared to move forward for what might be the outcome of it all but also not able to stop even for a second.</b> I was really dreading the end and it took me by surprise. I was highly impressed and satisfied with the entire book. There were a few things that I felt were unanswered but hey, we have a sequel and hence, I have really high expectations of the next book, especially because of the cliffhanger at the end which paves the way for an equally gritty and exciting sequel. Also, it has recently come to my knowledge that there is a Bok 1.5 as well-Iron to Iron, a novella about what exactly happened between Adele and Luka that <b>I HAVE BEEN DYING TO KNOW </b>but didn't get any answers about from the first book. So I am also excited about that. Lastly, there was one tiny thing that nagged at me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ According to Yael, here is no need to worry about Adele's parents because there are Resistance members waiting outside their houses to whisk them away to safety as soon as the mission is complete. However, what about Felix? Yael leaves him in her room, unconscious before going to the ball. How is he safe? He'd be caught in an instant and tortured to death for that. It's not so much as why did Yael do that as to why it didn't even occur to her that this is very risky. I am hoping the sequel has answers to that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>I'd also like to mention how <i>absolutely marvelous </i>the audio version of this book was.</b> The narrator, Christa Lweis really is the best that I have ever come across. Her voices for different characters, accents, tone, emphasis, and dramatics were immaculate. <i>It's amazing how a really good audio has the capability to tremendously increase the overall rating of a book.</i> I am not saying the book wasn't good by itself, but while the book rendered a gritty, fast-paced tale, it was also a little heavy on the description side. I don't particularly mind that sort of thing if it's done well, which by the way, it was. <b>However, the dialogue-paragraph scale was heavily tipped on the latter side. </b>I imagine that kind of thing might have gotten a little draining, especially where the thoughts of the protagonist get very repetitive at times, had I been reading the book. But the narrator knows her way with these descriptions. <br /><br />Not once did I find the flowery descriptions, loaded with metaphors and repetitive parts draining. Instead, it felt like the most natural thing. The narrator has a flair for making even the boring bits dramatic, packing even the repetitions and long purple prose with so much emotion that it pulls you in even more rather than pushing you away from it. I always used to be wary of audiobooks because I had put my own way of reading and interpreting dialogues and the overall essence of a particular moment on a pedestal and would think the narrator wouldn't be able to match that. But Christa Lewis surprised me even more by making the things that would have probably sounded boring in my head if I was reading by myself so much more interesting with her narration. <b>Hence, I would wholeheartedly recommend the audiobook of this book to anyone who wishes to pick this book in the future. </b>(Which by the way you totally should. The entire purpose of this review is to convince you to read the book.)<br /><br /><blockquote> <i>“Her self-reflection was no reflection at all. It was a shattered mirror. Something she had to piece together, over and over again. Memory by memory. Loss by loss. Wolf by wolf.” </i> </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7081081680282869626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SoFCa3yoL7cVjb8Hcln46aUNCvDEHWF77Au/gX2EYgjnQqIUkBohwTe+fDMBTdiZ4k7y/C0h8Ugr4xOiYrDOgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oJH5+NfkOFq64Ih9/JT3Y0mNJ+Zc3XbP1U90xveebkgNUhmHO1Y2LJjTS0mPgNcTDs7f6rXh5vwSp9jl6KrCwQ==')})
  }
